Feasibility Study Report

3.2. Question 2. To make assessment of O&M costs, cost for technical service and replacement of
components

3.2.1. M&O costs for PV system consists of three major parts:

Part 1 is cost of the current technical service of PV system;
Part 2 is cost of the current and mid-term repairing of the components used for PV system;
Part 3 is M&O costs for PV system that are needed for planned replacement of its components

•
•
•
based on their lifetime.

3.2.2. Current technical service of PV system includes:

•
•
•
•

current technical service of PV panel;
current technical service of connecting lines and switching devices composing the PV system;
technical service of accumulators;
technical service of electronic devices such as inverter and controller.

3.2.2.1. Current technical service of PV panels is the regular and regulated cleaning their surfaces
from pollutions, snow and ice as well as cleaning and preventive measures for contacts and electrical
wires available at the PV modules. Frequency, amount, regulations and technology of the technical
service of the PV panels have to be indicated in the relevant M&O.

3.2.2.2. Current technical service of the connecting lines and switching devices included into the PV
system package has to be made in accordance with the requirements stated in the Regulations on
Technical Operation and Regulations on Safety Measures (official publishing house of the State Power
Inspectorate “UZGOSENERGONADZOR, Tashkent, 2005). The service includes regular cleaning
and tightening the contacts, periodical checking the switching and connecting devices, all types of
fuses, surface of the connecting wires, their insulation, etc. As soon the inadequacies are identifies, the
relevant measures to be undertaken during the current technical service.

3.2.2.3. Current technical service of all types of accumulators is first of all to maintain clean surface
of the accumulators’ bodies and regular cleanup of their clamps.

3.2.2.3.1. In case if the PV system is equipped with the open-type accumulators, amount of the
technical service is quite large, it requires higher qualification of the staff, and use of special materials
(distilled water, sulphuric acid, etc.).

To illustrate the above said, a quote from the Regulations on Technical Service for the open-type
accumulators manufactured by the VHB Firm is cited below:

To ensure efficient operation of the batteries, the following activities shall be implemented:

Monthly:

Visual control of electrolyte’s level and external surface of the batteries.

•
Water shall be added not latter than the electrolyte’s level will reach the lowest permissible level fot
the electrolyte. Operational temperatures above 20 0C and often charges at the increased voltage
increase water consumption. To add water, distilled water that meets the requirements for cleaning
given in Table 4, shall be used only;

Control of voltage level for constant recharging at the rectifier;

•
• Temperature control in the premises;
• Testing operational efficiency of the ventilation system;
• Control of electrolyte’s density:
a)
b)

Selectively for 10% of accumulators,
For accumulators at which the reduced voltage took place during the previous annual testing.

Annually:

Control of voltage at all accumulator batteries. The allowable variation at particular

1.
accumulators can be -0.05/+0.1 V of the rated voltage;

Control of the electrolyte’s density at all accumulators. The allowable variation at particular

2.
accumulators can be ± 0.01 g/cm3 of the rated value.

Note:

138

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

1.
rate, they shall be checked monthly;

In case of voltage fluctuation at particular accumulators for the value greater the allowable

2.
greater the allowable rates, they shall be replaced.

In case of voltage and electrolyte density fluctuations at some accumulators for the values

Once during 3 years capacities of all accumulators of the battery shall be checked in the mode of the
constant recharge by the same current as was used during the commissioning.

3.2.2.3.2. For the sealed-in accumulators, the amount of technical service is essentially less. As an
example, the instruction for technical service for such accumulators manufactured by the TOP
POWER Firm, can be used:

Once during 6 months to check voltage of the battery as well as the temperature and voltage at the
monitoring elements, and results shall be registered in the accumulator registry.

Once a year to check the battery’s voltage, and temperature and voltage at each element of the battery,
and results shall be registered in the accumulator registry.

3.2.2.3.3. Comparing the content of the sections 3.2.2.3.1. and 3.2.2.3.2., it is obvious that technical
service of the sealed-in accumulators is essentially simpler, it doesn’t require higher qualification of
the staff and use of special materials. This is one of the main reasons that usage of sealed-in
(unattended) accumulators has been recommended as a technical solution for PV system proposed for
RHCs in the section 4.2 of Report 4.

3.2.2.4. Current technical service of electronic devices (controller and inverter) is a periodic checking
fulfillment of their main functions (according to the operational regulations), cleaning their surfaces,
cleanup the clamps and contacts.

3.2.2.5. Comparison of the scope of works on the technical service indicated in the sections 3.2.2.3 –
3.2.2.4. with data given in the “Unified tariff and qualification reference-book on works and
occupations” (Edition 1, Section: occupations for workers general for all sectors of economy.
Publishing house “Mashinostroenie”, Moscow, 1986) has showed that all above mentioned works
have to be implemented by a technician of RHC that shall have qualification ‘Electrician on repairing
and service of electrical equipment’ of the second or third qualification grades. Taking into
consideration that this staff member will be very likely the only one specialist of such qualification at
the site (RHC), it would be preferably that the person has the third qualification grade.

3.2.2.6. According to the “Unified 22 grade scale for wages and salaries” applied in Uzbekistan, an
electrician on repairing and service of electrical equipment of the third grade has monthly wage of
approximately 44 ths UZS (approx. 35USD) as of 01.08. 2007. Therefore, cost of the current
technical service of PV systems is 420 USD per year.

3.2.3. Costs of the current and medium repairing of the components with which the PV system is
equipped with, is mainly the costs of possible repairing the controller and inverter.

The upper limit for the costs of their repairing can be approximately estimated the following way:

3.2.3.1. According to the data given in Table 1.1 of Report 4, RHCs are not supplied with power
during approximately 30% of the time, or about 2,500 hours per year. This means that time of active
operation of the PV system is 2,500 hours per year, or 25,000 hours during 10 years.

3.2.3.2. Controller and inverter include about 200 electronic devices that operate during 5*106 of
device-hours during 10 years. If it is assumed that an average intensity of breakdowns for electronic
components is λ~10-6 1/h, the number of breakdowns will be equal to 5 breakdowns during 10 years of
operation or one breakdown during 2 years of operation.

3.2.3.3. Based on assessment made by the experts of JSC FOTON, cost of one repairing work for one
sophisticated electronic device is in average 2.5-5% of its total cost. Costs of controller and inverter
are 2,000 USD for the base option and 1,100 USD for the alternative option (see Table 1.7 of
Additions to Report 4). Therefore, cost of one repairing can be 30-100USD, or in average about
60USD per one repairing work. As the frequency of electronic equipment breakdowns can be
forecasted as 1 breakdown during 2 years, the costs of its repairing will be about 30 USD per year.

3.2.4. Costs of planned replacement of PV system components

This primarily includes replacement of accumulators, if their lifetime is less 10 years.

139

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

3.2.4.1. Accumulators proposed for PV system can be installed in RHC (see Table 1.3 of Additions to
Report 4) have declared lifetime of 7 years. Therefore, accumulators shall be replaced once during 10
years of accumulators’ operation. Thereby, costs of their replacement during 10 years will be in the
amount stated in Table 1.4 of Additions to report 4.

3.2.4.2. Actually, industries manufacture the sealed-in (unattended) accumulators with declared
lifetime of 10 and more years. At the same time, their price differs by 30% from the price for similar
accumulators with declared lifetime of 5 years.

In particular, a firm “VYBOR” offers an accumulator of GPL 121000 type (Manufacturer: Company
CSB Battery Co., Ltd. Taiwan) with voltage of 12 V, capacity of 100 A*h, and lifetime of 10 years for
225USD. But the price for similar accumulator of GP 121000 type with lifetime of 5 years
manufactured by the same company is 180USD. Thus, price difference is not more 30%.

3.2.4.3. it is obvious that use of more expensive accumulators with the declared lifetime of 10 years
for PV systems is more economical valuable. At the same time, taking into consideration that the share
of cost of accumulators in the total cost of the PV system is not exceed 20% (see Table 1.7 of
Additions to Report 4), total cost of PV system will be increased not more than 6-7%. Such approach
allows avoiding replacement of accumulators and, therefore, expenses required for planned
replacement of accumulators. In this case, total M&O costs for PV system to be installed in RHC
will be 450 USD per year (see sections 2.1.6. and 2.2.3.).

Feasibility Study Report

Feasibility Study Report

Annex 6. Reports of National Consultant/Expert on
supply and demand side improving, Mr. Petr
Pozychanyuk

Data, Analysis and Recommendations

General Data
The following documents had not been submitted: certificate for equipment installed in RHC,
statement from electric inspection authorities on RHC equipment conditions, dielectric rigidity
testing certificate of wire and cable lines, earth connection testing certificate.

We assume that these issues are OK (Assumption)

Statistics data show that RHC work 3,648 hours annually out of 8,760 possible hours constituting a
year.

According to international consultant and materials collected by National Expert on PV-systems the
RHC equipment mainly works part-time during a day. For extraordinary cases like power-offs or
blackouts, the equipment with power consumption of 500 W would enable main functions of RHC.
To enable more functions the 5 kW equipment would be needed. The issue of averaged data on
energy consumption, which is repeated in many tables, can be considered as some sort of
controversial question when it refers to assessment of power of energy generating equipment. This is
because of the fact that even short-time consumption of peak load values, when frequently repeated,
requires values of power of generating equipment, therefore power load (consumer) can not be
drastically decreased.

This averaged data can show only changes in costs, say for fuel, if diesel or petrol generator is used,
or in recourses of accumulator batteries in terms of charge depth of discharge to asses its’ service
life.

I.Technical Solutions on Five Rural Health Centers
1.A.Umarov Rural Health Center (RHC)

According to Consultant on PV-systems full power consumption is equal to 6,300/14,300 W.
Probably energy generating equipment with the power of 7,000/15,000 W could be needed to meet
the requirements.

Under such conditions the issue of integration into existing internal RHC network could be
simplified.

The most unreliable period of power supply lasts from November till March. This is 5 month or 125
days = 1,500 working hours. Occasional (extraordinary) blackouts – 168 hours (7 days).

Provisionally the most frequently blackout periods can be assumed as 6 hours. However we may
also assume it to be longer. Provisionally blackout period can be assumed as up to 2 days.

Conclusions on A. Umarov RHC:
- main power feed is considered as unreliable.
- Blackouts may happen almost every day and could last for long periods.
(this fact has an impact on technical solutions using electric power accumulating systems, as no
reliable data available on precise periods of absence of power in industrial electric networks)

-

the most appropriate option for A. Umarov RHC seems to be independent source of power, such
as diesel or petrol generator, with small-capacity UPS to use during start of generator.

148

Feasibility Study Report

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196
-

In order to use medical refrigerator during blackouts an automatically controlled generator to
switch on/off power shall be needed.

- There is no fundamental difficulty in this issue, except significant difference in equipment price.

Technical Solution on A. Umarov RHC

Option 1.

а) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 6 hours during blackouts, for
equipment with the capacity up to 500 W the UPS Liebert UPStation GXT2 – 10 kWA can be used
(capacity is a bit overstated due to starter current of the used equipment and rugged environment)
for temporary (emergency) power supply, or similar one.

If the UPS serves for more than one consumer than the issue of cable configuration shall be sorted
out and warning system shall be enabled to inform about UPS conditions (for instance about
accumulator capacity) if consumers located in different rooms (offices).

Features: After 6 hours of operation the UPS (as source of power) needs to be charged. It can be
used again as independent source of power after 8-10 hours. During this time recharging of the UPS
shall be arranged (it is possible to use diesel (petrol) generator of adequate power).

The issue of lighting can be solved through portable sources of light (lanterns or lamps with
accumulators). It is possible to use LED stationary or portable lamps, however the latter proposal
is still under consideration as no data available about its’ reliability, though according to the
manufacturer lamps’ service life is almost 10,000 hours with 5 times less power consumption than
luminescent energy saving lamp)*.

According to our experience the service life is about 3-5 years.

b) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 6 hours during blackouts, for RHC
equipment with the capacity up to 5 kW the automatic power generator run by petrol or diesel
depending on price & quality, which will be automatically switched on\off during blackouts shall be
needed. Generator capacity is 5-8 kW (more precise capacity figures can be calculated during
voltage surges on RHC loads)

It is also necessary to sort out the issue of cable configuration to enable connection of equipment of
particular importance excluding possibilities of unforeseen connections. The issue of protecting
power supply from short circuits and overloads. For sure, this issue may be covered by using UPS
10 kVA х 6 or UPS up to 50 kVA capacity with built-in diesel-generator, however the cost of such
decision very far exceeds $10,000 and we even can not consider such option.

Features: The generator requires periodical maintenance, providing with fuel and spare parts, as
well as specific place for installation. Special fire and safety precautions should be followed.
Generator service life depends on number of hours worked and measured by moto\hours. This figure
is around 5,000 moto\hours.

Option 2.
a) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 2 days during blackouts, for RHC
equipment with the capacity up to 500 watt the automatic power generator with the capacity up to 1
kilowatt run by petrol, which will be automatically switched on\off during blackouts shall be needed
(depending on medical equipment requirements UPS with the capacity up to 500 kVA shall be used
together). During blackouts it will work only during RHC’s staff labor hours.

b) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 2 days during blackouts, for RHC
equipment with the capacity up to 5 kW, it is recommended to use diesel generator (DG) with the
capacity of 8-10 kW. When needed individual UPS shall be arranged for (capacity up to 1,000 VA).
It will also work only during RHC’s staff labor hours

followed.

N. Baymuhammedov Rural Healthcare (RHC)
Total power consumption is 7,800/16,000 Watt. Probably it would be necessary to use energy
generating equipment with the capacity up to 10\20 kilowatt, which would simplify the issue of
integration into internal RHC network.

Feasibility Study Report

The most unreliable period of power supply lasts from November till March. This is 5 month or 125
days = 1,500 working hours. Occasional (extraordinary) blackouts – 168 hours (7 days).

There are complaints on power quality: 40% of the time the voltage is low (160-170 volt) causing
dysfunction most of the equipment. More detailed study of such low voltage is needed. Such voltage
can be considered as blackout. Probably voltage stabilizers could be used to improve the voltage
quality but it seems to be questionable solution and should be checked.

Conclusions on A.Umarov RHC: According to data presented by National Consultant on PV-
systems the voltage level is low (up to 40% of time) therefore voltage stabilizers shall be added into
the system, but this solution needs to be analyzed and checked.

Power corresponds to load (up to 500 watt and 5 kilowatt)

а) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 6 hours during blackouts, for
equipment with the capacity up to 500 watt power supply schemes similar to the schemes of power
supply from PV-systems can be used. But instead of solar panels rectifying installation with
corresponding automatic control device to switch on\off alternative power supply.

This solution is acceptable for 6 hours blackouts as well as for
b) blackouts with the duration up to 2 days. The difference is in capacities of accumulator batteries
and its’ power. Also automatic network control device shall be added.

3.1 Johanobod Rural healthcare (RHC)

It is located in mountain area, 1,500 m above sea level (for this altitude electro-technical standards
for the altitude of above 1,000 m shall be applied , as water boils under temperature of 950С, internal
combustion engine power losses are around 20% that increases fuel consumption per generation of 1
kWh of energy, etc.)

Working hours: around-the-clock work
It is possible significant power consumption for washing and ironing.

There are in-patient hospital consisting of 6 wards and maternity ward in the RHC.

Total power consumption is 17,000 Watt. Probably it would be necessary to use energy generating
equipment with the capacity up to 20 kilowatt, which would simplify the issue of integration into
internal RHC network.

The most reliable period of power supply lasts from November till March. This is 5 month or 125
days = 1,500 working hours.

According to the data presented by National Expert on PV-systems the power supply is not reliable
with high probability of sudden outage in any time of RHC operation for unpredicted periods.

3.2 Conclusions on Jahonobod RHC
Option 1.
a) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 6 hours during blackouts, for
equipment with the capacity up to 500 kW the automatic power generator with the capacity up
between 600-1,000 W run by petrol, which automatically controls power supply during blackouts,
can be used. There is no low-capacity generators run by petrol with automatic power supply control
device available in Uzbekistan. Therefore generator shall be started manually. Usually prepared
generator can be started within 2-3 minutes. Substitution of power supply blackouts can be arranged
through UPS with capacity of 1,000 VA.

Characteristics: During blackouts power supply shall be switched to independent supply source,
i.e. petrol generator. In this case it is not desirable to use automatic device due to significant power
consumption by automatic commutation control device and its’ high price.

The generator requires periodical maintenance, daily inspections, and providing with fuel and spare
parts, as well as specific place for installation. Special fire and safety precautions should be
followed. Generator service life depends on number of hours worked and measured by moto/hours.
This figure is around 5,000 moto/hours.
(Usually this data are not shown by the manufacturer)

b) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 6 hours during blackouts, for RHC
equipment with the capacity up to 5 kW the automatic power generator run diesel with the capacity
of 8-10 kW shall be needed. The capacity figures presented to meet reliability of power supply.

The device shall be connected to internal network of the specified equipment to enable no-break
power supply. (Possible connections in accordance with three-phase or one-phase schemes – shall

152

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196
be clarified during designing in accordance actual power supply cabling layout of RHC building
facilities)

Feasibility Study Report

Characteristics: This technical solution would require special outside building place for installation
the generator. Special fire and safety precautions should be followed as well as ensuring fire
protection of stored fuel. Special staff training shall be needed.
Option 2.
a) In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 2 days during blackouts, for RHC
equipment with the capacity up to 500 W the automatic power generator with the capacity up to
2 kW run by petrol, with automatic power supply control device shall be needed (depending on
medical equipment requirements UPS with the capacity up to 1,000 VA shall be used).

Characteristics: the same like in the sub-section a) of the Option 1

In order to ensure reliable power supply for the period up to 2 days during blackouts, for RHC
equipment with the capacity up to 5 kW, it is recommended to use diesel (petrol) generator with the
capacity of 8-10 kW. The capacity figures presented to meet reliability of power supply.

b) Or 2 generators working by turns with automatic control can be used during blackouts in the
network with the capacity of up to 6 kW (if there is a probability of blackout for the period of
more than 2 days) with the possibility of joint work of two generators when needed. In this case
cabling layout is complicated and special commutation and protection systems shall be used.

The device shall be connected to internal network of the specified equipment to enable no-break
power supply. (Possible connections in accordance with three-phase or one-phase schemes – shall
be clarified during designing in accordance actual power supply cabling layout of RHC building
facilities).

Characteristics: This technical solution requires special outside building place for installation the
generator. Special fire and safety precautions should be followed as well as ensuring fire protection
of stored fuel. In case of installation of two generators the layout of the equipment shall be arranged
in a way allowing maintenance activities during functioning one of the devices. The staff shall be
properly trained.

4.1 Pakhtakor rural healthcare (RHC)

There is an electric pump with the power consumption of up to 1 kW in the RHC. Total power

153

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196
consumption is 15,100 W. The issue would be solved through installation of diesel generator with
the capacity of 16 kW ** with automatic control device. This would simplify the issue of integration
into internal RHC network.

Feasibility Study Report

The most unreliable period of power supply lasts from September till April. During the most period
of diseases peaks (8 month of the year) power supply is particularly unreliable.

Based on available power supply reliability data independent (non-depending from networks)
sources of power supply shall be used.

4.2 Conclusions on Pakhtakor RHC

Due to similar conditions for this RHC the abovementioned options on improving reliability of
power supply to RHC (A. Umarov, N. Baymuhammedov, Jaohanobad, but mainly independent) can
be used (under power consumption of 500 W, 5 kW)

5.1 Juzim-Bog Rural Healthcare (RHC)

Total power consumption is 12,450 W. Probably it is necessary to use energy generating equipment
with the capacity up to 15 kW, which would simplify the issue of integration into internal RHC
network.

The most unreliable period of power supply lasts from November till May. During the most period
of diseases peaks ( 8 month of the year) power supply is particularly unreliable.

According to the presented data for Juzim-Bog RHC independent source of power supply shall be
needed. This solution was already considered for all of the RHCs described above.

For Juzim-Bog RHC the solution combining PV-system equipment with infeed from industrial
network seems to be interesting. Rectifying installation and protection unit shall be added to the PV.
In principle, this technical solution can be applied to all of the RHCs. In accordance with the
requirements (for 6 hours as well as 2 days blackouts) this task can be completed by making
corresponding adjustments to battery capacities and output power. JSC Foton can easily implement
such solution. The reliability of the system would significantly improve.

Capacity of proposed equipment increased by 1.3 – 1.5 times due to absence of accurate information
on:

- Temperature inside the room by season (i.e. no data). There is a possibility of improper heating
in winter. When it is cold, accumulators’ capacity considerably decreases, that is the reason for
increase.

-

In summer, increase is caused by high temperature which adversely affects to resource of
accumulators and electronic modules of equipment. There is a possibility of breakdown at
ultimate operation, power reserve of modules, therefore, is needed.

The second factor is more rational use of resource of equipment. For the most accurate calculation,
it would be efficient to prepare several variants with full-scale tests in real conditions. Then, on the
basis of obtained data, design should be prepared for technical, and if required. For construction part
of the system which provide reliable power supply to RHC. General design, obviously, should
comprise all aspects of power supply, namely electric power, heating, hot and cold water supply,
etc.

table below:

Table with the data on Uzbek market potential and component parts needed for the implementation
of technical solutions.

China &
Uzbekistan
Russia

Proposed components comply with ISO 9001 – 2000 (and has appropriate certificate issued by
relevant authority). Sellers of equipment have corresponding licences for business.

It is reasonable that procurement of equipment from little known company is risky at some extent.
Firstly, because of implementation of guarantees, secondly, in provision of spare parts in post
guarantee period. To this end, before taking decision on procurement of equipment, it would be
better to examine data on manufacturer, which type of equipment and to whom it was supplied, and
references; how servicing of equipment supplied and being supplied is carried out and company’s
age. Careful approach in selection of supplier would allow to a greater extent eliminate risks.

In this case, it is optimal to find a supplier, who based on TOR, would be able to supply equipment,
provide its commissioning and secure warranty. Additionally, by separate contract it would provide
equipment maintenance works

Arrangement of equipment servicing

There are no servicing companies that could service the proposed equipment for reliable power
supply to RHC based on proposed technologies (apart from factory made UPS) in Uzbekistan at
present.

All mobile companies and communication companies have servicing centres for similar equipment.
On the analogy of works, servicing centres for air conditioners, refrigerators and other sophisticated
consumer electronics can be reviewed. Usually, these are organised by manufacturers. There are no
problems with spare parts and deliverables, as well as with consumables, at properly organised
servicing centre. Personnel commonly are trained at the premises of manufacturer; they have all
equipment required for testing and maintenance, and issues of transportation and communication are
addressed. There are branches of servicing centre in each province. Works are implemented on the
basis of guarantee and contracts.

In principle, there are companies that could provide servicing, but they put conditions of having a
significant number of objects, uniformity of type of equipment at RHC, i.e. from a limited number
of suppliers. Lack of required calculated figures and data made it impossible to assess cost of
servicing works, production, human resources, transportation, etc. (probably, servicing and
installation issued can be dealt by Foton Ltd., Akkumenergo or any other company, but without
specific proposal I have not had a possibility to discuss those issues with the managers of above
companies).

The Ministry of Health might have a division on maintenance of medical equipment, which can deal
with the matter of equipment for reliable power supply to RHC. Each province should have
branches on maintenance of medical equipment.

Installation costs

With regard to installation of equipment, it can be said that for implementation of those works an
electrician of medium qualification if needed (graduated from electrotechnical college), who can

163

Feasibility Study Report

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196
deal with technical documents, equipment supplied and capable to understand diagrams,
experienced in operating of internal-combustion engines and mechanisms. The electrician would
need an assistant (perhaps, from amongst RHC staff). Scope of works subject to equipping with all
component parts and installation tool will take 3-5 days of erection and commissioning, even if the
most complex technology proposed for RHC is used. Funding of this activity would not exceed
Soum 250,000 (only salary, per diems, and transportation). Costs of materials should be prepared
based on technical design and installation drawings. Separate specifications of materials, equipment
and component parts need to be prepared for each specific item.

There are certainly some technologies which practically do not require any specific works, similar,
say, to switching on the TV-set or any other electrical appliance.

Operational costs

Operational costs (conditionally without labour) include consumables, high-wear parts, as well as
broken-down parts during operation of equipment. Let us consider operational costs of benzine
(gasoline) generator:

-

-

-

fuel, oil

filters (air, fuel, etc.)

ignition device

There are data on replacement of individual parts and components for running hours as per
specification and reference book. (there is a specific list for each item)

Therefore at claimed value of 5000 motor/h, it is possible to calculate approximate list of required
spare parts.

Similar approach for other equipment:

-

-

consumables

spare parts

It is not difficult to make calculations of consumables for each type of equipment, but for spare parts
field experience would be required. Normally, service centres could provide information during
execution of servicing contract.

Cost estimates for 20 years (tentative).

1. Petrol generator has 5000 motor/h. At operation 500 hours a year in average, its resource is 10
years. (Of course, frequent turning on the motor could notably decrease the resource. However,
it would be considered that operation was in normal mode). Hence, for the period 20 years, 1
replacement of petrol generator is needed.

2. Life time of (resource of reliable operation) electronic modules (inverters, controllers, rectifiers)
relay and switching device – 10 years. Hence, for the period of 20 years, 1 replacement is
needed.

3. Accumulators. For starter batteries, period of 2 years are accepted as a life time. For the period

of 20 years, 9 replacements are needed.

Batteries for accumulation of power for UPS* has 5-7 years resources. Hence, for the period of
20 years, 3-4 replacements are needed.

It is appropriate mention here that high temperature has an adverse impact on all accumulators.
Long operation at ambient temperature higher than 30-350С, reduces accumulators’ resource by
half. Generally, certificates shows the resource, when accumulator works at 20-250С, and
further a schedule of resource reduction is given based on temperature and duration of operation

164

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

in different conditions. As such, resource might be significantly less, and more frequent
replacement would be needed.

4. UPS in Uzbekistan’s conditions, when climatic requirements are not observed has resources for

3-5 years. For the period of 20 years, replacement should be done 4 – 6 times.

5.

Life time of wire and cable lines – 10 years. For the period of 20 years, 1 replacement is
needed.

These data should be considered during preparation of feasibility study in future costs section.

Assessment of capacities of RHC personnel to operate equipment on reliable power supply

In order to use equipment, RHC personnel should have certain training.

1. All people involved in operation of electric equipment should have to be trained in use of
equipment and should pass technical test to allow working with equipment up to 1000V with
relevant classification group, in accordance with existing safety requirements and obtaining of
certificate of standard pattern. For RHC, office instructions and recommendations should be
worked out on the basis of current regulations and standards of Rules of Electricity Installation
and Rules of Safety Work.

2. During mass installation of equipment for RHC, it is desirable to organise training in examining
of equipment for reliable power supply to RHC and practical skills on its operation and
maintenance. At the end training, test shall be conducted and certificates of completion issued.

Attention is also drawn to the fact that RHC is an independent entity and as such can add to its staff
list a position of a part time electrician (perhaps, a number of RHCs located in vicinity from each
other would have had one electrician for equipment maintenance). In any event, RHC personnel
need to be trained and prepared.

Energy saving

Task of electricity supply reliability and matter of energy saving contradict with each other. All
equipment accumulating energy or transforming it, say DC into AC or AC into DC, have in essence
cost component. Irrespective of accepted technology, i.e. at goal-setting of improved reliability, we
are doomed beforehand to have increased energy costs, rather than in the case of good power
supply. That depends on efficiency of equipment applied. However, even at application of the most
efficient equipment with reliable power supply, cost of power consumed from autonomous sources
increases at least by 1.5 times.

Things are even worth with energy generating equipment, such as petrol generators, diesel
generators, turbo-alternators, etc. Costs of production of electrical energy from such energy
generating equipment for guaranteeing of high level of power supply reliability are much more
expensive than from the grid.

In this case, would it be more practical to use the state-of-the-art equipment for energy saving? But
this, as a rule, leads to significant rise in price of equipment applied. Apparently, for resolving the
issue of energy saving, it is necessary to make a compromise by weighing the level of requirement
and adequacy, and also practicability adoption of any technology.

Conclusion

Issues of provision of reliable power supply, put in assignment, are urgent. Improving reliability of
power supply is addressed worldwide and immediate in resolving.

I would like to express my opinion on priority level of provision of RHC with highly reliable power
supply equipment. Foremost issue is lighting, next one is equipment for sterilization medical tools

165

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196
and refrigerators for storage of medicaments, and the third one is all other equipment. Based on
these views, I have prepared my technical solutions (I would suggest to discuss this issue).

Feasibility Study Report

However, for certain RHC it is necessary to investigate and eliminate reasons of non-reliable grid.
Nevertheless, something could be done to improve this situation. Even minor reliability growth
would greatly reduce the price of applied technology. It is necessary to randomly revise the lines,
substations for clarification of objective reasons of shutdowns and dumps, and seek for clear
response from district power grid.

This report covers all issued of assignment based on data submitted by the project manager.

1. Introduction

Selection of Hot-Water Supply for Rural Health Care

According to hot water consumption rates (KMK 2.04.01-98) and having in mind local conditions, a RHC would require 150-250 liters of hot water
per day.

Let us consider RHC hot water supply through electrical water heaters (option I) and solar collectors (option II).

2. Technical Features

2.1. Electrical water heater: - possibility of generation of significant volumes of hot water under low-capacity electric wiring and comparatively
low power inputs, which is one of the features of electric water heaters (EWH). Its’ power consumption varies between 1,2 to 2,5 kilowatt, though it
is time consuming process to prepare significant volumes of hot water. (200 liters – 5-8 hours), The design of EWH enables to store the heated water
hot without big power inputs.

Users safety and life time of EWH depend on its’ proper installation. Installation regulations determined by ГОСТ/GOST Р 50571 “Buildings
Electrical Installations, Electrical Code” and manufacturers’ recommendations.

182

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

Life time of electric water heater is 8-10 years. During this period a turbular electric heating element is to be replaced 2 or 3 times.

2.2.

Solar Energy Collecting Panel

Solar energy collecting panel is intended for individual houses, farms, pastures, health-improving, social and other facilities. The device can operate
in field conditions without water supply system as it can be filled in by any available water from any source. When the device is connected to water
pipeline/ watertank, water is supplied automatically as needed through special valve.

The device consists of solar collector with integral reservoir-heat exchanger. Primary coolant circuit contains antifreeze or ethylene glycol solution.
Heating of potable water is arranged in a tank through the heat exchanger. Such collector works all the year round. Under cloudy weather the water is
heated up to 60-65ºС through turbular electric heating element which is integrated into reservoir-heat exchanger. This enables to save up to 70% of
energy annually.

Solar energy collecting panel is to be installed on roof horizontally on-the-mitre 40-42 º towards south. Connection to hot water supply system is
made through using two tubes.
Life time is 15-20 years. Glass and antifreeze (ethylene glycol) are to be replaced during operational time as needed.

3. Calculation of Heat and Energy Consumption.

Conclusions

Capital investments for procurement and installation of solar collector are $375 higher. However, operating costs for solar collectors would be 65%
lower, and thus, in 2.5-3 years additional capital investments into solar collectors would be fully recovered, and its following operation would be two
times cheaper than electric water heater’s one.

The calculations made under the cost of 1 kilowatt of UZS 43.7. Having in mind annual increase of power costs, during 2-3 years the power costs would
increase by 1.5-2 times, which will result in constant growth of operating costs.

Feasibility Study Report

The design of pilot batch of solar panels developed by JSC FOTON under UN Project UZB/03/001 has high efficiency and maximally corresponds to
technical characteristics of European analogs:

• An absorber has a high coefficient of efficiency of transformation of solar energy into thermal energy;
• Panel is not heavy and designed to have effective heat insulation.
• 1 m2 of solar panel can produce 1 Gkal of heat which corresponds to 18,000 liters of hot water with a temperature of 60 °С.
• 136 m3 of natural gas is needed to produce the same amount of hot water. With lost in networks actual volumes of needed gas would amount

180 м3.

• Cost of 1 Gkal of heat from centralized heating system is UZS 13,968.

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

Conclusions (additional)

1.
In order to improve reliability of RHC hot water supply electric water accumulator tanks with the capacity of up to 50-120 liters can be used.
Heated water can be stored for a long period in well-isolated tank. Installed capacity of electric heating elements of 1.2-2 kilowatt enables storage of
water heated up to 65°С within 4-8 hours.

In order to enable continuous hot water supply gas water accumulator tanks can be also use. They have the same advantages like electric ones.

2.
Heating is done through popping of gas with automatics ensuring maintenance the temperature at the same level.

In order to improve reliability solar water heaters with collector area of 1 m2 and tank capacity of 80 liters can be installed; or with collector
3.
area of 2 m2 and tank capacity of 160 liters. Solar water heaters can be used seasonally or whole-year. Seasonal solar water heaters are of very simple
design and low cost. Solar water heaters for whole-year’ use are of double-loop circuit with turbular electric heating element in accumulator tank
which enables to maintain constant temperatures under low solar radiation.

4.

All these options can be recommended for using in RHCs depending on operational conditions (reliability of gas supply, power supply, etc.)

Solar- fuel boiler

К 10 – Heat exchanger

К 1 – Fuel Boiler

К 15 – Tank with antifreeze

Solar-fuel boiler is to be installed in RHC and comprises the following parts: gas boiler, solar panels with heat exchanger, accumulator tank with heat
exchangers. The system consists of three circuits, equipped with automatic control system. Solar modules with the total area of 16 m2 may be installed either
on roof or ground. The device is designated for hot water and heating supply. In summer time hot water supply is arranged through solar collectors. In autumn-
spring periods solar collectors can preliminary heat water for boiler.

К 11 – Solar Panel
К 4 – Accumulator Tank
with heat
exchangers

Replacement of natural gas with solar energy allows to save annually 60 – 70 % of fuel.

4. Relevant to lifetime

Main parameters of RHCs

“Djeykhanabad”

‘Umarov”

“N. Baymukhamedov”

“Pakhtakor”

“Juzim-Bog”

Self-made natural gas firing boilers are installed in all these RHCs. The Ministry of Healthcare
has to replace them with more efficient boilers. To avoid large investments it is proposed the
three following options:
1. Installation of natural gas burner with automatic device for safety measures, and insulation of
pipes located inside the boiler house.
2. Replacement of the existing boilers with new energy efficient boilers with automatic devices
for safety and regulation.
3. Replacement of the existing boilers with new energy efficient boilers with automatic devices
for safety and regulation. This system has to be equipped with regulation of temperature inside
the premises using temperature sensors (thermostats). The radiators have to be also replaced.

Renewable source of energy:
- solar
- wind
- hydropower
- biomass
- geothermal
- earth heat

Gas vessels

Increasing gas pressure in pipes

In A.Umarov and N.Baymuhamedov RHCs boilers can
be shifted to liquefied gas. However, there are no
conditions to store liquefied gas in the RHCs (in terms
of fire safety requirements and requirements of
Gostechnadzor [local state engineering supervision
authority]).
According to neighboring residents, starting from
December 10 up to February 10 gas pressure in
pipelines decreased down to 50-60 mm In A.Umarov
and N.Baynuhamedov RHCs.
This happens because the RHCs are located at the ends
of gas supply lines, and there is no possibility to
“loopback the pipelines” – to connect two different
branches of gas pipeline to make a loop for improving

Data on financing RHC in Uzbekistan

o Mechanism for RHC Budget Formation

Budget for every Region (Oblast) is a subject of approval at the national level, whereupon it is
approved at corresponding Regional sessions of local authorities. After identification of key figures
(budget) regional health authorities work out average budget expenses per capita, which forms a
basis for individual RHCs.

For instance: under average per capita on-budget expenditure of UZS 4,395 the total RHC budget
would be 6 592,5 thousand sum.

• Who makes decisions (RHC, at Regional or National level) and based on what

principles:

o Allocation of annual RHC Budget:

RHC Manager makes decisions over annual budget allocations with the concurrence of Regional
Health Protection authorities.

o Staff number and hiring physicians and nurses, and their salaries:

Staff list is developed in accordance with the regulations set up at the national level, and is a subject
of approval and endorsement by Regional Health Protection authorities during the preparation of
budget cost estimates. RHC Managers makes decisions over the issues of staff hiring, setting up
their terms of reference and salaries.

o RHC Working Hours:

Working hours for staff members are set in accordance with national regulations: for physicians and
middle level medical staff - 6 hours; outpatient reception hours of dentists – 5.5 hours; for
exodontists – 6 hours, non-medical staff – 7 hours. However, RHC and staff working hours are set at
the local level and can be different, so called “floating schedule”, but shall be within timetables
established in accordance with Uzbekistan Labor Code (40 working hours a week for one staff
member).

• Financing of Procurement and Replacement of Equipment and Lighting Devices, and

Equipment Maintenance and Repairs

Financing of procurement and replacement of equipment and lighting devices, equipment
maintenance and repairs are arranged based on leftover principle. First priority is given to financing
of staff salaries, then medicaments, public utilities and RHC economic expenditures as last priority.

• Statistics or averaged data on public utilities expenses in different types of RHCs (type

1, type 2, ...), for the last 3 years:

(notice: RHCs in Tashkent region were financed together with Central District Hospitals.
Since 2007 they have separate budget)

• What RHC or regional authorities can afford in terms of rehabilitation of power

supply system and re-equipment of heating system and hot water supply

There is a number of activities on rehabilitation and re-equpment of power supply, heating, and hot
water supply systems being carried out by authorities in every region. These activities are also will
be implemented in the future. However due to limited RHC budgets the abovementioned activities
mainly are being implemented (and shall be carried out) at the expense of centralized investments,
partially at the expense of sponsors and attracted investors.

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

What are the different criteria which define each type? Is there a criterion linked with utilities?
Period of heating for different provinces?

Duration of period of heating according decree of Cabinet Ministers - 154
days, but local administrations may correct it depending on the weather.
Heating season starts from 15 October every year.

How do they regulate temperature inside RHC?

Staff of RHC regulates boilers operation. Gas supply is increased in
mornings and decreased after RHC closed. Also boilers work is regulated
during working hours.

Construction materials, nb of doors and windows. Are there everywhere insulation of ceiling
(type of insulation) and what for roofs, walls, floor, windows, doors?

Insulation of roofs and ceiling is local – clay. The rest is insulated by staff of
RHC at the beginning of heating period.

Types, efficiency and average age of boilers for heating, for hot water.

Average age of boilers is 4 -5 years, boilers – self-made with capacity from
20 liters to 100 liters.

Types and power/capacity of gas meters and electricity meters.

In RHC it is mainly installed:
gas meters type RG – 10 with capacity 10 m3 / hour;
electricity meters type SACHU 3 phase with capacity 380 volt.

What are the reactions of RHC concerning failure of gas, electricity or water? How do they
manage shortage of gas on one side, of electricity on another side?

Of course reaction is negative. When gas shortage they use coal, wood and
liquid fuel. RHC staff use self-made electric heaters.

Are frequency and duration of shortage different from one province to another?

Yes it is different. In Tashkent region shortages happen less frequently than
in others.

Can we identify different types of failures for gas, electricity and water supply?

It is possible to do it approximately, but to define it exactly it is needed to
provide a monitoring.

Are there problems of quality of gas (low pressure) and of electricity (voltage, frequency)?

Yes such problems exist: low gas pressure in winter time, and low voltage.

Concerning equipment, is there or could it be a political/ecological approach for choice of
equipment: label A for refrigerators instead of C, low consumption bulbs, laboratories
equipment with own batteries, etc

Yes, it is possible to use a political/ecological approach for choice of
equipment.

Are there any risks (if shortage of power or heating supply or low voltage and low pressure of
gas): beside finance loss; vaccines loss.

Yes, there are risks to lose vaccines due to electricity shortage, not proper
sterilization and bad disinfection of instruments.

It should be indicated priority medical equipment for emergency cases and equipment which
necessarily need electricity supply in the list of equipment from Health 2 project, its power
consumption should be also indicated.

Centrifuge – 300 W,

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

Annex 10. Reports of National Consultant/Expert on
energy economics, Ms. Elvira Bikeeva
Task 1. Cost Efficiency Analysis of the Proposed Options

on Improvement of RHC Power Supply

1.1. Brief analysis of the current pricing system in power supply sphere and identification

of possible increase of prices for main types of energy resources.

In order to estimate costs of energy efficiency for different options on improving reliability of RHCs
power supply, identification of its’ economic effects resulting from reduced fuel and power
consumption the following data is needed: prognostic parameters of pricing changes for main types
of energy resources, which would help to use data on dynamics of expected increase in adjusting
conditions of cost efficiency of investment projects implementation.

Thus, state policy on energy resources pricing at the stage of liberalization of economy during 2001-
2005 was focused on reduction of differentiation and transformation of internal market prices
towards its’ significant increase.

Average annual increase of tariffs for electricity during 2001-2005 was about 40-43% (for
comparison: during 1995-2000 - 5-5.5%). nominal values for oil and gas were increased by 26.4%
and 42.3% respectively (against of 5% and 3.7% during 1995-2000.) Dynamics of increasing of
prices for coal and crude oil slightly slowed down compared with the period of 1995-2000, but
remained relatively high - 31.1% and over 41.%.

These trends had an effect on growth rate, incomes and financial situation of fuel-energy complex
(FEC). Price increase resulted in some increase of profitability of power industry production from
negative 12.2% in 2000 up to 8-10% in 2004-2005, while in gas-and-oil producing industry the
situation stabilized at the level of 12-15%. High dynamics of growth of tariffs rates for industrial
customers and population had an effect on changes of price ratio of internal and world prices. If up
to 2000 this ratio was amounted around 10-15% of world level, then in 2004-2005 it constituted 53-
55%. The same trends could be observed in gas industry^ fixed price for gas up to 2000 was around
20% of world prices, while in 2005 – 33-35%.

To ensure stable operation of fuel-energy complex, in perspective, further step-by-step equalization
of internal prices of energy resources with the rate of self-financing production of main types of fuel
and energy resources is envisaged.

Experts estimation on local power industry sector investment needs during forthcoming 5-8 years
are amounted as much as $3.5 billions. Uzbekistan will have to meet 65-70% of these needs at own
expenses, which requires prices and tariffs are to be set at the level enough to cover production costs
and long-term investments.

In order to achieve this target, prices for gas during 2006-2010 shall be increased by 1.9 times, or
18-20% annually, which would result the prices to get close to the average world prices by 34.7
(see Table 1.1, 1.2).

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

development of energy saving potential. This means, that taking into account consumer qualities of
energy resources in terms of calorific efficiency, price for black oil (mazut) would be lower than
price for gas, which in its’ turn would be 30-35% higher than coal price. In power industry, which
is one of the large fuel consumers, competition between gas and coal can be possible only if coal
market price will be 15-35% lower than gas price. Having in mind consumption qualities of black
oil (mazut) fuel, its’ market price should be 5-10% lower than gas price.

Increase of prices for gas will be accompanied with increase of prices for power and district heating
supply, due to gas share of 75-80% in boiler-stove fuel during production of electricity and heating.
Thus, it is expected, that only due to increasing of prices for gas, electric power tariffs will be
increased not less than by 22-25%. Increasing of investment costs component in power industry
will be oriented the same direction. As a result, by 2010 prices for electric power shall be increased
by 1.5-1.6 times compared with the level of 2006. In accordance with the dynamics of expected
growth, price relations between internal and world prices for electric power shall be formed towards
its’ rapprochement – by 22.4. Internal market electric power tariffs shall form 90% of world level
(under world average value of the tariff – 0.05 dollar./ кkilowatt-hour) – see pic. 1.1.-1.2.

Preparation of data and preliminary calculation of total capital expenditures and operational
expenses on the options of increasing of reliability of RHC power supply

I.2 Improving of electric lighting of RHC
Introduction of more economical system of electric lighting is one of the main conditions of
effective implementation of measures on improving reliability of RHC power supply. It is also one
of the most important priorities in the system of measures on energy savings. In accordance with the
proposed technical decision total number of energy saving fluorescent lamps throughout of the
RHCs is 88 lamps. Total capital expenditures, depending on manufacturers’ price would be from
$616 up to $968, including operational costs at the amount of $176 (see Table 1.3.1).

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

The results of the tentative economic analysis showed the following:

- energy consumption after introduction of economical system of lighting is more than 3.8 times
lower than under traditional scheme of lighting.

- Introduction of energy saving luminous lamps would allow to save 5,462 kilowatt-hour of energy
annually, which constitutes 277,0 thousand sum ($218.6) under expected increase of electric power
tariffs up to 0,04 US dollar./kilowatt-hour

- Costs pay-back period for the introduction of modern lighting system would be 2.8 years (under
prices of lamps produced by local manufacturers) and 4.4 years (under prices of lamps produced by
European manufacturers) - this confirms economic efficiency of the proposed project decision.

- In terms of fuel, the savings would be 0,672 t.o.e or 585,1 cubic meters of natural gas.

1.3 Power supply for RHC:

Setting up of standby service is priority task in the system of measures to enhance the reliability of
power supply at RHC. Based on outcomes of analysis of existing problems in power supply,
studying of climatic and territorial properties of the regions basic technical solutions on
enhancement of reliability of their power supply were justified, providing for using as a whole of:
diesel or petrol generators with small UPS; accumulators; UPS; photovoltaic PV-systems. As a basis
of technical solutions given parameters on electric power used by RHC equipment during
emergency 500W to 5kW, daily consumption 3 kWh to 15 kWh were included. Summary of options
for enhancement of power supply reliability at RHC, assessment of capital costs for equipment and
operational costs are given in Table 1.3.1

gas, replaceable volume will be 105.5 m3 or 121.3 kg of equivalent fuel.

Feasibility Study Report

Main conclusions: Preliminary analysis of technical solutions directed for enhancement of reliability
of power supply at all RHC has shown that solutions providing for introduction of photovoltaic PV-
systems would be much more expensive than accumulators systems; UPS; diesel or petrol
generators with UPS, which value of efficiency index put together slightly higher. However, from an
economic point of view, all projects have low economic efficiency, and basically directed to
problems of enhancement of power supply reliability. At the same time, technical solutions have
positive social consequences, lying in reliability and improvement of provided services, rising of
level of population’s health. For improvement of economic efficiency index of technical solutions, it
is necessary to consider the options of power supply not only in emergency state, but also in
operating condition.

1.4 Improving RHC Heat Supply System

The following approach was used for preliminary calculation of cost efficiency and payback period
of capital expenditures for implementation of main technical solutions on improving efficiency and
reliability of heat supply to the five RHCs1:

- at the first stage maximal heat flow was identified – kilowatt

- consolidated indicator of heat flow for heating premises, which is around 125 Watt/m2

where:
according to Expert estimates

- factor of heat flow =0,25

А – Building area (data from the report)
- maximal heat loss of the heated premises in RHC in heat flow is not less than 40% of
(cording to Expert estimates)
- average monthly temperature during heating season for rural areas of Uzbekistan:
- in October - +12,50С
- in November - +5,00С
- in December - +0,00С
- in January - -2,20С
- in February - -0,20С
- in March - +5,60С

Average outside temperature for the considered period is +3,50С

- actual average heat loss in heated premises
=0,4
(180+200) – calculated temperature difference
(180-3,50)- actual average annual temperature difference during heating season
- total heat loss for heating season:

×(180+200) /(180-3,50)

=

×24×182

1.6. Data on stakeholders interested in implementation of projects on increasing of reliability
of rural health care (RHC) power supply:

At present institutional and regulative basis of power supply improvement in rural areas, energy
savings, introduction and development of non-traditional sources of energy are at relatively weak
level. From one hand there are many agencies and organizations involved in the process of
implementation of activities on energy savings and improving reliability of industrial energy and
power supply, including consumers from budgetary sphere.

From the other hand, the results of activities implemented by these organizations are not effective
enough, due to higher priorities, based on traditional sources of energy, set on tasks to ensure
sustainable dynamics of production of main types of energy resources, implementation of programs
on modernization and rehabilitation of large generating supply, sustainable energy supply of
strategically important industries.

However, power industry authorities recognize importance of necessary basic changes in energy
consumption sphere, importance of introduction of non-traditional sources of energy and
implementation of projects introducing more efficient and economically sound power supply
systems, particularly in rural areas as high-priority.

This direction is of particular importance in the framework of implementation of activities on
increasing quality of provided services, including medical ones, throughout the country. The
Government of Uzbekistan developed “Progarmme on Formation of Uniform Strategy of Territorial
Development of Uzbekistan for the Period of 2007-2011.” (Decree of Uzbek President dated April
20, 2006 # Р-2482 “On Formation of Commission for Development of Uniform Strategy for
Territorial Development of Uzbekistan for the Period of 2007-2011”), which pays significant
attention to the development of production and social infrastructure, increasing of qualitative
characteristics of power and water supply, transport, medical and other services ensuring decreasing
the level of regional differentiation in providing services and social benefits.

2 Umarov RHC – electric water heater
3 Used price for 1000. м3 gaz - 58 USD / Used price for 1000 m3 gaz - 105 USD
3 Payback Period with average world price for gaz 160$/ 100 m3 will be shorten significantly.

236

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

Therefore, the roles which play state, regional authorities and ministries in implementation of
Health-2 Project will become more important. International donor agencies make significant
contribution to the development of rural health care system and implementation of projects on
improving energy efficiency.

The main stakeholders involved into the implementation of projects on improving reliability of
power supply of rural health clinics (RHC) are as follows:

Смотровая гинекологии - Room for patients’ gynecological examination
Аптечный киоск - Drugstore stall
Акушер-гинеколог – Obstetrician-gynecologist
Ожидальная - Waiting room
Кабинет врача педиатра – Pediatrician room
Кабинет для прививок - Inoculation room
Кабинет патронажной медсестры - Health and visiting nurse room
Пандус - Ramp

Общая площадь – Total area is 624.4 m2
Нормируемая площадь - Area standardized is 537 m2
Строительный объем - Constructing amount is 2,848.5 m2

СВП – III типа на 75 посещений в смену с обслуживанием от 5000 до 7000 человек – The 3rd
type RHCs are considered for 75 visits per shift at serving from 5,000 to 7,000 persons

План действующего утвержденного проекта – Design of the approved and operating project

During 1999-2004, ‘Health-1’ Project aimed to strengthening and reforming the primary healthcare
system in Fergana, Navoiy, and Syrdaria provinced had been implemented. The second amendment
had been included into the loan agreement dated of 19 March 2003. According to the amendment,
shortage of water regions such as the Republic of Karakalpakstan and Khoresm province were
included into the “Health-1” project. This has been done due to savings made and without increase
of loan commitments made by the government.

The project objective was establishing demonstration models of the primary medical care services
on the basis of examples of Fergana, Navoiy, Syrdaria, and Khoresm provinces and the Republic of
Karakalpakstan.

Construction, reconstruction, and operation of RHCs and renovation of a set of medical institutions
located in the rural areas became a contribution made by Uzbekistan. Equipping the facilities with
medical equipment and medicines as well as personnel training and introduction of new mechanisms
for financing and management have been envisaged for use of the WB loan funds.

To achieve the above indicated goals and objectives, four major components were included into the
project’s structure:

• Strengthening services provided by the primary healthcare system;
• Training of doctors and nurses of general medical practice;

242

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

• Strengthening the system of management and financing applied for the primary healthcare

system;

• Management of the project.

The following activities were implemented within each component:

I.

Strengthening the primary healthcare system

In five regions of the country, activities on establishing a branched network of RHCs were
implemented. This allowed to simplify organization of the primary medical and sanitary aid (PMSA)
and shift from the many-staged (Medical Attendant and Obstetrical post, Rural Medical Ambulance
Station, Rural District Hospital, and Central Republican Hospital) to two-staged (RHC - Central
Republican Hospital) approach.

Total amount of RHCs equipped within the framework of the ‘Health-1’ project is 677. Among them
214 RHCs are located in Fergana province, 121 RHCs – in Syrdaria province, 89 RHCs – in Navoiy
province, 121 RHCs – in Khoresm province, and 108 RHCs – in Karakalpakstan. Moreover, 20
RHCs were equipped in Samarkand province based on the Uzbek Government suggestion.

To increase access for local population living in remote and isolated rural areas to medical services,
70 units of specialized off-highway vehicles of UAZ type cars and 28 DAMAS cars have been
procured and delivered by the project.

To provide emergency and first aids to rural population living in Navoiy and Syrdaria provinces, a
radio communication system that allows establishing an effective operational radio communication
with the remote and isolated RHCs located at these regions with district, provincial, and national
centers of emergency aid has been installed. 55 fixed and 16 mobile radio communication stations
have been installed in Navoiy province, and 39 fixed and 4 mobile radio communication stations
have been installed in Syrdaria province.

Results achieved

The evaluation of RHCs’ activities showed that actually in comparison with 1998 the number of
visits made to one RHC is increase in 2 times but the number of patients sent to consultations made
by specialized doctors has been decreased by 33.5%, patients sent to hospitals – by 26.8%. This
proves the increased trust and access of rural population to medical services provided by the RHCs.

Moreover, introduction of new approaches of management and financing the rural healthcare
facilities allowed:

•

• Shifting to more efficient financing system based on the amount of the population served
instead of the previous inefficient approaches based on the capacities of the medical
institutions such as number of personnel, area of facilities etc.;
Increasing budgets of the primary medical and sanitary aid (PMSA) due to reduction of
expenses for the secondary healthcare system. For instance, in Fergana province the relative
share of PMSA’s expenses was increased from 13.6% of the total expenses for the
healthcare to 24.3% in 2003. United personal standard was increased from 367 UZS in 1999
to 1,615 UZS in 2003;

• Allocating more resources for serving women and children due to use of sex and age factors

used to determine budget required for the PMSA’s facilities;

• Providing financial sustainability, autonomy and flexibility in management of funds and

personnel;
•
Increase motivation of PMSA’s suppliers in providing medical services to the population;
• Rationalization of the cost structure of budget funds. For example, share of costs allocated
for personnel’s wages and salaries was reduced from 56.3% in 1999 to 54.8% in 2003 but
funds allocated for medicines during the same time period were increased from 5.2% to
6.2%. Share of inefficient expenses dealt with payment of allowances for children that are
under 2 years.

243

UNDP- UZB -03 #00054196

Feasibility Study Report

Therefore, proper conditions have been established for the primary healthcare system, and new
system of medical aid based on the general medical practice is functioning successfully. This allows
having an efficient and quality medical aid for rural population in the nearest future.

The similar objectives on strengthening the primary healthcare system are being implemented by the
on-going ‘Health-2’ Project (2005-2009). Total number of RHCs equipping within the framework of
the project is 2,315 RHCs. It has to be emphases that according to the Resolution of the President of
Uzbekistan #PP-569 dated 18.01.2007 “On measures aimed to efficient usage of Japanese
Government grant provided for improving the primary healthcare system in Tashkent and Djizzak
provinces, and to improving medical nurses’ education”, 114 RHCs located in Tashkent and Djizzak
provinces will be equipped with medical equipment in 2007-2008. In total 3,106 RHCs.

1.2.1. Statistical data based on sizing and types of RHCs

According to the Annex, page 61

1.2.2. Statistical data based on location of RHCs

Number of RHCs located in mountain areas is 20-25% roughly.

Number of RHCs located in remote and isolated areas is 10% roughly.

1.3. How many RHCs are equipped by “Health-1’ and ‘Health-2’ projects?

Total amount of RHCs equipped within the framework of the ‘Health-1’ project is 677. Among
them 214 RHCs are located in Fergana province, 121 RHCs – in Syrdaria province, 89 RHCs – in
Navoiy province, 121 RHCs – in Khoresm province, and 108 RHCs – in Karakalpakstan.

Total amount of RHCs planed to be equipped within the framework of the ‘Health-2’ project over
the country is 2,330 (see Table 1).
